	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Henry VIII of England</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_VIII&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>)</span></div>

<p><b>Henry VIII</b> (28 June 1491 – 28 January 1547) was King of England from 1509 until his death in 1547. He was the second <a href="/wiki/House_of_Tudor" title="House of Tudor">Tudor monarch</a>, succeeding his father <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a>. Henry is best known for <a href="/wiki/Wives_of_Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Wives of Henry VIII">his six marriages</a>, in particular his efforts to have his first marriage (to <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>) annulled. His disagreement with the Pope on the question of such an annulment led Henry to initiate the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">English Reformation</a>, separating the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> from papal authority. He appointed himself the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Head_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Head of the Church of England">Supreme Head of the Church of England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">dissolved convents and monasteries</a>, for which he was <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_excommunicated_by_the_Catholic_Church" title="List of people excommunicated by the Catholic Church">excommunicated</a>. Henry is also known as "the father of the Royal Navy"; he invested heavily in the Navy, increasing its size greatly from a few to more than 50 ships.
</p><p>Domestically, Henry is known for his radical changes to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Constitution of the United Kingdom">English Constitution</a>, ushering in the theory of the divine right of kings. He also greatly expanded royal power during his reign. He frequently used charges of treason and heresy to quell dissent, and those accused were often executed without a formal trial by means of <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_attainder" title="Bill of attainder">bills of attainder</a>. He achieved many of his political aims through the work of his chief ministers, some of whom were banished or executed when they fell out of his favour. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Thomas Wolsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cromwell" title="Thomas Cromwell">Thomas Cromwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rich,_1st_Baron_Rich" title="Richard Rich, 1st Baron Rich">Richard Rich</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cranmer" title="Thomas Cranmer">Thomas Cranmer</a> all figured prominently in his administration.
</p><p>Henry was an extravagant spender, using the proceeds from the dissolution of the monasteries and acts of the Reformation Parliament. He also converted the money that was formerly paid to Rome into royal revenue. Despite the money from these sources, he was continually on the verge of financial ruin due to his personal extravagance, as well as his numerous costly and largely unsuccessful continental wars, particularly with King <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor_Charles_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Roman Emperor Charles V">Holy Roman Emperor Charles V</a>. At home, he oversaw the legal union of England and Wales with the <a href="/wiki/Laws_in_Wales_Acts_1535_and_1542" title="Laws in Wales Acts 1535 and 1542">Laws in Wales Acts 1535 and 1542</a>, and he was the first English monarch to rule as King of Ireland following the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Ireland_Act_1542" title="Crown of Ireland Act 1542">Crown of Ireland Act 1542</a>.
</p><p>Henry's contemporaries considered him an attractive, educated, and accomplished king. He has been described as "one of the most charismatic rulers to sit on the English throne".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> He was an author and composer. As he aged, however, he became severely obese and his health suffered, contributing to his death in 1547. He is frequently characterised in his later life as a lustful, egotistical, harsh, and insecure king.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He was succeeded by his son <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward VI">Edward VI</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaux_Passional_(f.9)._Henry_VIII_(Cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg/170px-Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="381" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg/255px-Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg/340px-Vaux_Passional_%28f.9%29._Henry_VIII_%28Cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="636" data-file-height="1427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaux_Passional_(f.9)._Henry_VIII_(Cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration from <i><a href="/wiki/Vaux_Passional" title="Vaux Passional">Vaux Passional</a></i> thought to show Henry (top) mourning his mother, with his sisters, Mary and Margaret, in the foreground, 1503</div></div></div>
<p>Born 28 June 1491 at the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Placentia" title="Palace of Placentia">Palace of Placentia</a> in Greenwich, Kent, Henry Tudor was the third child and second son of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crofton2006_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crofton2006-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>  Of the young Henry's six siblings, only three&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">Arthur, Prince of Wales</a>; <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Tudor_(queen_consort_of_France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary Tudor (queen consort of France)">Mary</a>&#160;– survived infancy.<sup id="cite_ref-Crofton2006a_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crofton2006a-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He was baptised by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Foxe" title="Richard Foxe">Richard Fox</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Exeter" title="Bishop of Exeter">Bishop of Exeter</a>, at a church of the <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Observant Franciscans</a> close to the palace.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick3_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick3-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1493, at the age of two, Henry was appointed Constable of <a href="/wiki/Dover_Castle" title="Dover Castle">Dover Castle</a> and Lord Warden of the <a href="/wiki/Cinque_Ports" title="Cinque Ports">Cinque Ports</a>. He was subsequently appointed <a href="/wiki/Earl_Marshal" title="Earl Marshal">Earl Marshal</a> of England and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lieutenant_of_Ireland" title="Lord Lieutenant of Ireland">Lord Lieutenant of Ireland</a> at age three, and was made a <a href="/wiki/Knight_of_the_Bath" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight of the Bath">Knight of the Bath</a> soon after. The day after the ceremony he was created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_York" title="Duke of York">Duke of York</a> and a month or so later made <a href="/wiki/Lord_Warden_of_the_Marches" title="Lord Warden of the Marches">Warden of the Scottish Marches</a>. In May 1495, he was appointed to the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Order of the Garter</a>. The reason for all the appointments to a small child was so his father could keep personal control of lucrative positions and not share them with established families.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick3_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick3-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Henry was given a first-rate education from leading tutors, becoming fluent in Latin and French, and learning at least some Italian.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Not much is known about his early life – save for his appointments – because he was not expected to become king.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick3_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick3-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In November 1501, Henry also played a considerable part in the ceremonies surrounding his brother's marriage to <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, the youngest surviving child of King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a> and Queen <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As Duke of York, Henry used the arms of his father as king, differenced by a <i>label of three points ermine</i>. He was further honoured, on 9 February 1506, by <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor_Maximilian_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian I">Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian I</a> who made him a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Golden_Fleece" title="Order of the Golden Fleece">Knight of the Golden Fleece</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1502, Arthur died at the age of 15, possibly of <a href="/wiki/Sweating_sickness" title="Sweating sickness">sweating sickness</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> just 20 weeks after his marriage to Catherine.<sup id="cite_ref-crofton126_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crofton126-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Arthur's death thrust all his duties upon his younger brother, the 10-year-old Henry. After a little debate, Henry became the new <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Cornwall" title="Duke of Cornwall">Duke of Cornwall</a> in October 1502, and the new <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> and Earl of Chester in February 1503.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Henry VII gave the boy few tasks. Young Henry was strictly supervised and did not appear in public. As a result, he ascended the throne "untrained in the exacting art of kingship".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henry VII renewed his efforts to seal a marital alliance between England and Spain, by offering his second son in marriage to Arthur's widow Catherine.<sup id="cite_ref-crofton126_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crofton126-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Both Isabella and Henry VII were keen on the idea, which had arisen very shortly after Arthur's death.<sup id="cite_ref-loades22_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades22-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June 1503, a treaty was signed for their marriage, and they were betrothed two days later.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick8_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick8-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A papal dispensation was only needed for the "impediment of public honesty" if the marriage had not been <a href="/wiki/Consummated" class="mw-redirect" title="Consummated">consummated</a> as Catherine and her <a href="/wiki/Duenna" class="mw-redirect" title="Duenna">duenna</a> claimed, but Henry VII and the Spanish ambassador set out instead to obtain a dispensation for "affinity", which took account of the possibility of consummation.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick8_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick8-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Cohabitation was not possible because Henry was too young.<sup id="cite_ref-loades22_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades22-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Isabella's death in 1504, and the ensuing problems of succession in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a>, complicated matters. Her father preferred her to stay in England, but Henry VII's relations with Ferdinand had deteriorated.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Catherine was therefore left in limbo for some time, culminating in Prince Henry's rejection of the marriage as soon he was able, at the age of 14. Ferdinand's solution was to make his daughter ambassador, allowing her to stay in England indefinitely. Devout, she began to believe that it was God's will that she marry the prince despite his opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-Loades2009_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loades2009-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_reign">Early reign</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HenryVIII_1509.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/HenryVIII_1509.jpg/170px-HenryVIII_1509.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/HenryVIII_1509.jpg/255px-HenryVIII_1509.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/HenryVIII_1509.jpg/340px-HenryVIII_1509.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1159" data-file-height="1762" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HenryVIII_1509.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eighteen-year-old Henry VIII after his <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> in 1509</div></div></div>
<p>Henry VII died on 21 April 1509, and the 17-year-old Henry succeeded him as king. Soon after his father's burial on 10 May, Henry suddenly declared that he would indeed marry Catherine, leaving unresolved several issues concerning the papal dispensation and a missing part of the <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">marriage portion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick8_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick8-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-loades24_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades24-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The new king maintained that it had been his father's dying wish that he marry Catherine.<sup id="cite_ref-Loades2009_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loades2009-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Whether or not this was true, it was certainly convenient. <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Maximilian_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Maximilian I">Emperor Maximilian I</a> had been attempting to marry his granddaughter (and Catherine's niece) <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Austria" title="Eleanor of Austria">Eleanor</a> to Henry; she had now been jilted.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Henry's wedding to Catherine was kept low-key and was held at the friar's church in Greenwich on 11 June 1509.<sup id="cite_ref-loades24_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades24-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June 1509, Henry led the now 23-year-old Catherine from the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> to <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> for their coronation, which took place the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick1819_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick1819-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> It was a grand affair: the king's passage was lined with tapestries and laid with fine cloth.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick1819_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick1819-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Following the ceremony, there was a grand banquet in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster Hall">Westminster Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> As Catherine wrote to her father, "our time is spent in continuous festival".<sup id="cite_ref-loades24_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades24-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two days after his coronation, Henry arrested his father's two most unpopular ministers, Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Empson" title="Richard Empson">Richard Empson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Dudley" title="Edmund Dudley">Edmund Dudley</a>. They were charged with <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">high treason</a> and were executed in 1510. Politically-motivated executions would remain one of Henry's primary tactics for dealing with those who stood in his way.<sup id="cite_ref-Crofton2006_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crofton2006-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Henry also returned to the public some of the money supposedly extorted by the two ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, Henry's view of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">House of York</a> – potential rival claimants for the throne – was more moderate than his father's had been. Several who had been imprisoned by his father, including the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Grey,_2nd_Marquess_of_Dorset" title="Thomas Grey, 2nd Marquess of Dorset">Marquess of Dorset</a>, were pardoned.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Others (most notably <a href="/wiki/Edmund_de_la_Pole,_3rd_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="Edmund de la Pole, 3rd Duke of Suffolk">Edmund de la Pole</a>) went unreconciled; de la Pole was eventually beheaded in 1513, an execution prompted by his brother <a href="/wiki/Richard_de_la_Pole" title="Richard de la Pole">Richard</a> siding against the king.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soon after, Catherine conceived, but the child, a girl, was <a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">stillborn</a> on 31 January 1510. About four months later, Catherine again became pregnant.<sup id="cite_ref-loades26_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades26-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On New Year's Day 1511, the child – <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Duke_of_Cornwall" title="Henry, Duke of Cornwall">Henry</a> – was born. After the grief of losing their first child, the couple were pleased to have a boy and festivities were held,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> including a two-day <a href="/wiki/Jousting" title="Jousting">joust</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/The_1511_Westminster_Tournament_Roll" title="The 1511 Westminster Tournament Roll">Westminster Tournament</a>. However, the child died seven weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-loades26_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades26-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Catherine had two stillborn sons in 1514 and 1515, but gave birth in February 1516 to a girl, <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary</a>. Relations between Henry and Catherine had been strained, but they eased slightly after Mary's birth.<sup id="cite_ref-loades4849_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4849-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Henry's marriage to Catherine has since been described as "unusually good",<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> it is known that Henry took mistresses. It was revealed in 1510 that Henry had been conducting an affair with one of the sisters of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Stafford,_3rd_Duke_of_Buckingham" title="Edward Stafford, 3rd Duke of Buckingham">Edward Stafford, 3rd Duke of Buckingham</a>, either Elizabeth or <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hastings,_Countess_of_Huntingdon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anne Hastings, Countess of Huntingdon">Anne Hastings, Countess of Huntingdon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The most significant mistress for about three years, starting in 1516, was <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Blount" title="Elizabeth Blount">Elizabeth Blount</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loades4849_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4849-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Blount is one of only two completely undisputed mistresses, considered by some to be few for a virile young king.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser1994_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser1994-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-loades4748_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4748-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Exactly how many Henry had is disputed: <a href="/wiki/David_Loades" title="David Loades">David Loades</a> believes Henry had mistresses "only to a very limited extent",<sup id="cite_ref-loades4748_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4748-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> whilst <a href="/wiki/Alison_Weir" title="Alison Weir">Alison Weir</a> believes there were numerous other affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> There is no evidence that Catherine protested, and in 1518 she fell pregnant again with another girl, who was also stillborn.<sup id="cite_ref-loades4849_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4849-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Blount gave birth in June 1519 to Henry's illegitimate son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Richmond_and_Somerset" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Richmond and Somerset">Henry FitzRoy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loades4849_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades4849-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The young boy was made Duke of Richmond in June 1525 in what some thought was one step on the path to his eventual legitimisation.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1533, FitzRoy married <a href="/wiki/Mary_FitzRoy,_Duchess_of_Richmond_and_Somerset" title="Mary FitzRoy, Duchess of Richmond and Somerset">Mary Howard</a>, but died childless three years later.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> At the time of Richmond's death in June 1536, Parliament was enacting the <a href="/wiki/Second_Succession_Act" title="Second Succession Act">Second Succession Act</a>, which could have allowed him to become king.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="France_and_the_Habsburgs">France and the Habsburgs</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/280px-British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/420px-British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/560px-British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5089" data-file-height="2461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_-_Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The meeting of Francis I and Henry VIII at the <a href="/wiki/Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold" title="Field of the Cloth of Gold">Field of the Cloth of Gold</a> in 1520</div></div></div>
<p>In 1510, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>, with a fragile alliance with the Holy Roman Empire in the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Cambrai" class="mw-redirect" title="League of Cambrai">League of Cambrai</a>, was winning a war against Venice. Henry renewed his father's friendship with <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII_of_France" title="Louis XII of France">Louis XII of France</a>, an issue that divided his council. Certainly war with the combined might of the two powers would have been exceedingly difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-Loades27_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loades27-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, however, Henry also signed a pact with Ferdinand. After <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a> created the anti-French <a href="/wiki/League_of_Cambrai#Holy_League" class="mw-redirect" title="League of Cambrai">Holy League</a> in October 1511,<sup id="cite_ref-Loades27_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loades27-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Henry followed Ferdinand's lead and brought England into the new League. An initial joint Anglo-Spanish attack was planned for the spring to recover <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a> for England, the start of making Henry's dreams of ruling France a reality.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The attack, however, following a formal declaration of war in April 1512, was not led by Henry personally<sup id="cite_ref-Scarisbrick2831_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scarisbrick2831-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and was a considerable failure; Ferdinand used it simply to further his own ends, and it strained the Anglo-Spanish alliance. Nevertheless, the French were pushed out of Italy soon after, and the alliance survived, with both parties keen to win further victories over the French.<sup id="cite_ref-Scarisbrick2831_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scarisbrick2831-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Henry then pulled off a diplomatic coup by convincing the Emperor to join the Holy League.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Remarkably, Henry had also secured the promised title of "<a href="/wiki/Most_Christian_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Most Christian King">Most Christian King</a> of France" from Julius and possibly coronation by the Pope himself in Paris, if only Louis could be defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg/220px-Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg/330px-Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg/440px-Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2175" data-file-height="2200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_VIII_with_Charles_Quint_and_Pope_Leon_X_circa_1520.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henry with <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> (right) and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a> (centre), c. 1520</div></div></div>
<p>On 30 June 1513, Henry invaded France, and his troops defeated a French army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Spurs" title="Battle of the Spurs">Battle of the Spurs</a> – a relatively minor result, but one which was seized on by the English for propaganda purposes. Soon after, the English took <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9rouanne" title="Thérouanne">Thérouanne</a> and handed it over to Maximillian; <a href="/wiki/Tournai" title="Tournai">Tournai</a>, a more significant settlement, followed.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Henry had led the army personally, complete with large entourage.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> His absence from the country, however, had prompted his brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV of Scotland</a>, to invade England at the behest of Louis.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, the English army, overseen by Queen Catherine, decisively defeated the Scots at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Flodden" title="Battle of Flodden">Battle of Flodden</a> on 9 September 1513.<sup id="cite_ref-loades63_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades63-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Among the dead was the Scottish king, thus ending Scotland's brief involvement in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-loades63_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades63-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> These campaigns had given Henry a taste of the military success he so desired. However, despite initial indications, he decided not to pursue a 1514 campaign. He had been supporting Ferdinand and Maximilian financially during the campaign but had received little in return; England's coffers were now empty.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> With the replacement of Julius by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a>, who was inclined to negotiate for peace with France, Henry signed his own treaty with Louis: his sister Mary would become Louis' wife, having previously been pledged to the younger Charles, and peace was secured for eight years, a remarkably long time.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> ascended the thrones of both Spain and the Holy Roman Empire following the deaths of his grandfathers, Ferdinand in 1516 and Maximilian in 1519. <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> likewise became king of France upon the death of Louis in 1515,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> leaving three relatively young rulers and an opportunity for a clean slate. The careful diplomacy of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Cardinal Thomas Wolsey</a> had resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1518)" title="Treaty of London (1518)">Treaty of London</a> in 1518, aimed at uniting the kingdoms of western Europe in the wake of a new Ottoman threat, and it seemed that peace might be secured.<sup id="cite_ref-loades6869_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades6869-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Henry met Francis I on 7 June 1520 at the <a href="/wiki/Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold" title="Field of the Cloth of Gold">Field of the Cloth of Gold</a> near <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> for a fortnight of lavish entertainment. Both hoped for friendly relations in place of the wars of the previous decade. The strong air of competition laid to rest any hopes of a renewal of the Treaty of London, however, and conflict was inevitable.<sup id="cite_ref-loades6869_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loades6869-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Henry had more in common with Charles, whom he met once before and once after Francis. Charles brought the Empire into war with France in 1521; Henry offered to mediate, but little was achieved and by the end of the year Henry had aligned England with Charles. He still clung to his previous aim of restoring English lands in France, but also sought to secure an alliance with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Burgundy" title="Kingdom of Burgundy">Burgundy</a>, then part of Charles' realm, and the continued support of Charles.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A small English attack in the north of France made up little ground. Charles <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">defeated and captured Francis at Pavia</a> and could dictate peace; but he believed he owed Henry nothing. Sensing this, Henry decided to take England out of the war before his ally, signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_More" title="Treaty of the More">Treaty of the More</a> on 30 August 1525.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Annulment_from_Catherine">Annulment from Catherine</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n,_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg/170px-Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg/255px-Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg/340px-Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n%2C_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1294" data-file-height="1682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catalina_de_Arag%C3%B3n,_por_un_artista_an%C3%B3nimo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, Henry's first queen</div></div></div>
<p>During his first marriage to <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, Henry conducted an affair with <a href="/wiki/Mary_Boleyn" title="Mary Boleyn">Mary Boleyn</a>, Catherine's <a href="/wiki/Lady-in-waiting" title="Lady-in-waiting">lady-in-waiting</a>. There has been speculation that Mary's two children, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Carey,_1st_Baron_Hunsdon" title="Henry Carey, 1st Baron Hunsdon">Henry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Carey" title="Catherine Carey">Catherine Carey</a>, were fathered by Henry, but this has never been proved, and the King never acknowledged them as he did Henry FitzRoy.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 1525, as Henry grew more impatient with Catherine's inability to produce the male heir he desired,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crofton51_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crofton51-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> he became enamoured of <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Mary Boleyn's sister, Anne</a>, then a charismatic young woman of 25 in the Queen's entourage.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Anne, however, resisted his attempts to seduce her, and refused to become his mistress as her sister Mary Boleyn had.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> It was in this context that Henry considered his three options for finding a dynastic successor and hence resolving what came to be described at court as the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_%22great_matter%22" class="mw-redirect" title="King&#39;s &quot;great matter&quot;">King's "great matter"</a>. These options were legitimising Henry FitzRoy, which would take the intervention of the pope and would be open to challenge; marrying off Mary as soon as possible and hoping for a grandson to inherit directly, but Mary was considered unlikely to conceive before Henry's death; or somehow rejecting Catherine and marrying someone else of child-bearing age. Probably seeing the possibility of marrying Anne, the third was ultimately the most attractive possibility to the 34-year-old Henry,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and it soon became the King's absorbing desire to annul his marriage to the now 40-year-old Catherine.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> It was a decision that would lead Henry to reject papal authority and initiate the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">English Reformation</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1491_Henry_VIII.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/1491_Henry_VIII.jpg/170px-1491_Henry_VIII.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/1491_Henry_VIII.jpg/255px-1491_Henry_VIII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/1491_Henry_VIII.jpg/340px-1491_Henry_VIII.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1213" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1491_Henry_VIII.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henry, c. 1531</div></div></div>
<p>Henry's precise motivations and intentions over the coming years are not widely agreed on.<sup id="cite_ref-elton103_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton103-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Henry himself, at least in the early part of his reign, was a devout and well-informed Catholic to the extent that his 1521 publication <i><a href="/wiki/Assertio_Septem_Sacramentorum" class="mw-redirect" title="Assertio Septem Sacramentorum">Assertio Septem Sacramentorum</a></i> ("Defence of the Seven Sacraments") earned him the title of <i><a href="/wiki/Fidei_Defensor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fidei Defensor">Fidei Defensor</a></i> (Defender of the Faith) from Pope <a href="/wiki/Leo_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo X">Leo X</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-elton75_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton75-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The work represented a staunch defence of papal supremacy, albeit one couched in somewhat contingent terms.<sup id="cite_ref-elton75_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton75-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It is not clear exactly when Henry changed his mind on the issue as he grew more intent on a second marriage. Certainly, by 1527 he had convinced himself that in marrying Catherine, his brother's wife, he had acted contrary to <a href="/wiki/Leviticus" class="mw-redirect" title="Leviticus">Leviticus</a> 20:21,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(canon_law)" title="Affinity (canon law)">impediment</a> Henry now believed that the Pope never had the authority to dispense with. It was this argument Henry took to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> in 1527 in the hope of having his marriage to Catherine annulled, forgoing at least one less openly defiant line of attack.<sup id="cite_ref-elton103_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton103-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In going public, all hope of tempting Catherine to retire to a nunnery or otherwise stay quiet was lost.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Henry sent his secretary, <a href="/wiki/William_Knight_(statesman)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Knight (statesman)">William Knight</a>, to appeal directly to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> by way of a deceptively worded draft papal bull. Knight was unsuccessful; the Pope could not be misled so easily.<sup id="cite_ref-Elton109_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elton109-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other missions concentrated on arranging an ecclesiastical court to meet in England, with a representative from Clement VII. Though Clement agreed to the creation of such a court, he never had any intention of empowering his legate, <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Campeggio" title="Lorenzo Campeggio">Lorenzo Campeggio</a>, to decide in Henry's favour.<sup id="cite_ref-Elton109_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elton109-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> This bias was perhaps the result of pressure from <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, Catherine's nephew, though it is not clear how far this influenced either Campeggio or the Pope. After less than two months of hearing evidence, Clement called the case back to Rome in July 1529, from which it was clear that it would never re-emerge.<sup id="cite_ref-Elton109_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elton109-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> With the chance for an <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulment</a> lost and England's place in Europe forfeit, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Cardinal Wolsey</a> bore the blame. He was charged with <i><a href="/wiki/Praemunire" title="Praemunire">praemunire</a></i> in October 1529<sup id="cite_ref-Lockyer2014_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lockyer2014-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and his fall from grace was "sudden and total".<sup id="cite_ref-Elton109_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elton109-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Briefly reconciled with Henry (and officially pardoned) in the first half of 1530, he was charged once more in November 1530, this time for treason, but died while awaiting trial.<sup id="cite_ref-Elton109_65-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elton109-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> After a short period in which Henry took government upon his own shoulders,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a> took on the role of Lord Chancellor and chief minister. Intelligent and able, but also a devout Catholic and opponent of the annulment,<sup id="cite_ref-Losch2002_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Losch2002-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> More initially cooperated with the king's new policy, denouncing Wolsey in Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A year later, Catherine was banished from court, and her rooms were given to Anne. Anne was an unusually educated and intellectual woman for her time, and was keenly absorbed and engaged with the ideas of the Protestant Reformers, though the extent to which she herself was a committed Protestant is much debated.<sup id="cite_ref-gunn_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gunn-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Warham" title="William Warham">William Warham</a> died, Anne's influence and the need to find a trustworthy supporter of the annulment had <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cranmer" title="Thomas Cranmer">Thomas Cranmer</a> appointed to the vacant position.<sup id="cite_ref-Losch2002_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Losch2002-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This was approved by the Pope, unaware of the King's nascent plans for the Church.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_to_Anne_Boleyn">Marriage to Anne Boleyn</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England#Reformation" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England §&#160;Reformation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_boleyn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anne_boleyn.jpg/170px-Anne_boleyn.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anne_boleyn.jpg/255px-Anne_boleyn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anne_boleyn.jpg/340px-Anne_boleyn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2401" data-file-height="3150" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_boleyn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a>, Henry's second queen; a later copy of an original painted c. 1534</div></div></div>
<p>In the winter of 1532, Henry met with Francis I at Calais and enlisted the support of the French king for his new marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Immediately upon returning to <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">Dover</a> in England, Henry, now 41, and Anne went through a secret wedding service.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> She soon became pregnant, and there was a second wedding service in London on 25 January 1533. On 23 May 1533, Cranmer, sitting in judgment at a special court convened at <a href="/wiki/Dunstable_Priory" title="Dunstable Priory">Dunstable Priory</a> to rule on the validity of the king's marriage to Catherine of Aragon, declared the marriage of Henry and Catherine null and void.  Five days later, on 28 May 1533, Cranmer declared the marriage of Henry and Anne to be valid.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Catherine was formally stripped of her title as queen, becoming instead "princess dowager" as the widow of Arthur. In her place, Anne was crowned <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_consorts" class="mw-redirect" title="List of English consorts">queen consort</a> on 1 June 1533.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The queen gave birth to a daughter slightly prematurely on 7 September 1533.  The child was christened <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth</a>, in honour of Henry's mother, Elizabeth of York.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the marriage, there was a period of consolidation taking the form of a series of statutes of the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation_Parliament" title="English Reformation Parliament">Reformation Parliament</a> aimed at finding solutions to any remaining issues, whilst protecting the new reforms from challenge, convincing the public of their legitimacy, and exposing and dealing with opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Although the canon law was dealt with at length by Cranmer and others, these acts were advanced by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cromwell,_1st_Earl_of_Essex" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Cromwell, 1st Earl of Essex">Thomas Cromwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Audley,_1st_Baron_Audley_of_Walden" title="Thomas Audley, 1st Baron Audley of Walden">Thomas Audley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Howard,_3rd_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas Howard, 3rd Duke of Norfolk">Duke of Norfolk</a> and indeed by Henry himself.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> With this process complete, in May 1532 More resigned as Lord Chancellor, leaving Cromwell as Henry's chief minister.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Succession_1533" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Succession 1533">Act of Succession 1533</a>, Catherine's daughter, Mary, was declared illegitimate; Henry's marriage to Anne was declared legitimate; and Anne's <a href="/wiki/Issue_(legal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Issue (legal)">issue</a> was decided to be next in the line of succession.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Supremacy" title="Acts of Supremacy">Acts of Supremacy</a> in 1534, Parliament also recognised the King's status as head of the church in England and, with the <a href="/wiki/Act_in_Restraint_of_Appeals" class="mw-redirect" title="Act in Restraint of Appeals">Act in Restraint of Appeals</a> in 1532, abolished the right of appeal to Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> It was only then that Pope Clement took the step of <a href="/wiki/Excommunication" title="Excommunication">excommunicating</a> Henry and Thomas Cranmer, although the excommunication was not made official until some time later.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;nb 3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The king and queen were not pleased with married life. The royal couple enjoyed periods of calm and affection, but Anne refused to play the submissive role expected of her. The vivacity and opinionated intellect that had made her so attractive as an illicit lover made her too independent for the largely ceremonial role of a royal wife and it made her many enemies. For his part, Henry disliked Anne's constant irritability and violent temper. After a <a href="/wiki/False_pregnancy" title="False pregnancy">false pregnancy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a> in 1534, he saw her failure to give him a son as a betrayal. As early as Christmas 1534, Henry was discussing with Cranmer and Cromwell the chances of leaving Anne without having to return to Catherine.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Henry is traditionally believed to have had an affair with <a href="/wiki/Margaret_and_Mary_Shelton" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret and Mary Shelton">Margaret ("Madge") Shelton</a> in 1535, although historian <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Fraser" title="Antonia Fraser">Antonia Fraser</a> argues that Henry in fact had an affair with her sister <a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelton" title="Mary Shelton">Mary Shelton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser1994_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser1994-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Opposition to Henry's religious policies was quickly suppressed in England. A number of dissenting monks, including the first <a href="/wiki/Carthusian_Martyrs" title="Carthusian Martyrs">Carthusian Martyrs</a>, were executed and many more <a href="/wiki/Pillory" title="Pillory">pilloried</a>. The most prominent resisters included <a href="/wiki/John_Fisher" title="John Fisher">John Fisher</a>, Bishop of Rochester, and Sir Thomas More, both of whom refused to take the oath to the King.<sup id="cite_ref-elton192_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton192-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Neither Henry nor Cromwell sought to have the men executed; rather, they hoped that the two might change their minds and save themselves. Fisher openly rejected Henry as the Supreme Head of the Church, but More was careful to avoid openly breaking the Treason Act, which (unlike later acts) did not forbid mere silence. Both men were subsequently convicted of high treason, however – More on the evidence of a single conversation with <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rich" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Rich">Richard Rich</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solicitor_General_for_England_and_Wales" title="Solicitor General for England and Wales">Solicitor General</a>. Both were duly executed in the summer of 1535.<sup id="cite_ref-elton192_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton192-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>These suppressions, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Lesser_Monasteries_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of the Lesser Monasteries Act">Dissolution of the Lesser Monasteries Act</a> of 1536, in turn contributed to more general resistance to Henry's reforms, most notably in the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage_of_Grace" title="Pilgrimage of Grace">Pilgrimage of Grace</a>, a large uprising in northern England in October 1536.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Some 20,000 to 40,000 rebels were led by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aske_(political_leader)" title="Robert Aske (political leader)">Robert Aske</a>, together with parts of the northern nobility.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Henry VIII promised the rebels he would pardon them and thanked them for raising the issues. Aske told the rebels they had been successful and they could disperse and go home.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Henry saw the rebels as traitors and did not feel obliged to keep his promises with them, so when further violence occurred after Henry's offer of a pardon he was quick to break his promise of clemency.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The leaders, including Aske, were arrested and executed for treason. In total, about 200 rebels were executed, and the disturbances ended.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Execution_of_Anne_Boleyn">Execution of Anne Boleyn</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein,_the_Younger,_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-Hans_Holbein%2C_the_Younger%2C_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2994" data-file-height="4203" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein,_the_Younger,_Around_1497-1543_-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henry c. 1537</div></div></div>
<p>On 8 January 1536 news reached the king and the queen that Catherine of Aragon had died. The following day, Henry dressed all in yellow, with a white feather in his bonnet.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The queen was pregnant again, and she was aware of the consequences if she failed to give birth to a son.  Later that month, the King was unhorsed in a tournament and was badly injured; it seemed for a time that his life was in danger. When news of this accident reached the queen, she was sent into shock and miscarried a male child that was about 15 weeks old, on the day of Catherine's funeral, 29 January 1536.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> For most observers, this personal loss was the beginning of the end of the royal marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the Boleyn family still held important positions on the Privy Council, Anne had many enemies, including the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Brandon,_1st_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="Charles Brandon, 1st Duke of Suffolk">Duke of Suffolk</a>. Even her own uncle, the Duke of Norfolk, had come to resent her attitude to her power. The Boleyns preferred France over the Emperor as a potential ally, but the King's favour had swung towards the latter (partly because of Cromwell), damaging the family's influence.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Also opposed to Anne were supporters of reconciliation with Princess Mary (among them the former supporters of Catherine), who had reached maturity. A second <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulment</a> was now a real possibility, although it is commonly believed that it was Cromwell's anti-Boleyn influence that led opponents to look for a way of having her executed.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2012_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2012-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anne's downfall came shortly after she had recovered from her final miscarriage. Whether it was primarily the result of allegations of conspiracy, adultery, or witchcraft remains a matter of debate among historians.<sup id="cite_ref-gunn_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gunn-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Early signs of a fall from grace included the King's new mistress, the 28-year-old <a href="/wiki/Jane_Seymour" title="Jane Seymour">Jane Seymour</a>, being moved into new quarters,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and Anne's brother, <a href="/wiki/George_Boleyn,_Viscount_Rochford" class="mw-redirect" title="George Boleyn, Viscount Rochford">George Boleyn</a>, being refused the Order of the Garter, which was instead given to <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Carew_(courtier)" title="Nicholas Carew (courtier)">Nicholas Carew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Between 30 April and 2 May, five men, including Anne's brother, were arrested on charges of treasonable adultery and accused of having sexual relationships with the queen. Anne was also arrested, accused of treasonous adultery and incest. Although the evidence against them was unconvincing, the accused were found guilty and condemned to death. George Boleyn and the other accused men were executed on 17 May 1536.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> At 8&#160;am on 19 May 1536, Anne was executed on <a href="/wiki/Tower_Green" title="Tower Green">Tower Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Marriage_to_Jane_Seymour.3B_domestic_and_foreign_affairs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_to_Jane_Seymour;_domestic_and_foreign_affairs">Marriage to Jane Seymour; domestic and foreign affairs</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:366px;max-width:366px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:160px;max-width:160px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour,_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/158px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="158" height="254" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/237px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/316px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4241" data-file-height="6824" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg/200px-Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="254" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg/300px-Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg/400px-Family_of_Henry_VIII_c_1545_detail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1906" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Jane_Seymour" title="Jane Seymour">Jane Seymour</a> (left) became Henry's third wife, pictured at right with Henry and the young <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England">Prince Edward</a>, c. 1545, by an unknown artist. At the time that this was painted, Henry was married to his sixth wife, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Parr" title="Catherine Parr">Catherine Parr</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>The day after Anne's execution in 1536 the 45-year-old Henry became engaged to Seymour, who had been one of the Queen's <a href="/wiki/Ladies-in-waiting" class="mw-redirect" title="Ladies-in-waiting">ladies-in-waiting</a>. They were married ten days later.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> On 12 October 1537, Jane gave birth to a son, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England">Prince Edward</a>, the future Edward VI.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The birth was difficult, and the queen died on 24 October 1537 from an infection and was buried in Windsor.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The euphoria that had accompanied Edward's birth became sorrow, but it was only over time that Henry came to long for his wife. At the time, Henry recovered quickly from the shock.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Measures were immediately put in place to find another wife for Henry, which, at the insistence of Cromwell and the court, were focused on the European continent.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With Charles V distracted by the internal politics of his many kingdoms and external threats, and Henry and Francis on relatively good terms, domestic and not foreign policy issues had been Henry's priority in the first half of the 1530s. In 1536, for example, Henry granted his assent to the <a href="/wiki/Laws_in_Wales_Acts_1535%E2%80%931542" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws in Wales Acts 1535–1542">Laws in Wales Act 1535</a>, which legally annexed <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, uniting England and Wales into a single nation. This was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Succession_Act" title="Second Succession Act">Second Succession Act</a> (the Act of Succession 1536), which declared Henry's children by Jane to be next in the line of succession and declared both Mary and Elizabeth illegitimate, thus excluding them from the throne. The king was also granted the power to further determine the line of succession in his will, should he have no further issue.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> However, when Charles and Francis made peace in January 1539, Henry became increasingly paranoid, perhaps as a result of receiving a constant list of threats to the kingdom (real or imaginary, minor or serious) supplied by Cromwell in his role as spymaster.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Enriched by the dissolution of the monasteries, Henry used some of his financial reserves to build a series of coastal defences and set some aside for use in the event of a Franco-German invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_to_Anne_of_Cleves">Marriage to Anne of Cleves</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_of_Cleves,_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg/170px-Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg/255px-Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg/340px-Anne_of_Cleves%2C_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1506" data-file-height="2016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_of_Cleves,_by_Hans_Holbein_the_Younger.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Cleves" title="Anne of Cleves">Anne of Cleves</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger" title="Hans Holbein the Younger">Hans Holbein the Younger</a>, 1539</div></div></div>
<p>Having considered the matter, Cromwell, now Earl of Essex, suggested <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Cleves" title="Anne of Cleves">Anne</a>, the 25-year-old sister of the <a href="/wiki/William,_Duke_of_J%C3%BClich-Cleves-Berg" title="William, Duke of Jülich-Cleves-Berg">Duke of Cleves</a>, who was seen as an important ally in case of a Roman Catholic attack on England, for the duke fell between <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger" title="Hans Holbein the Younger">Hans Holbein the Younger</a> was dispatched to Cleves to paint a portrait of Anne for the king.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Despite speculation that Holbein painted her in an overly flattering light, it is more likely that the portrait was accurate; Holbein remained in favour at court.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> After seeing Holbein's portrait, and urged on by the complimentary description of Anne given by his courtiers, the 49-year-old king agreed to wed Anne.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> However, it was not long before Henry wished to annul the marriage so he could marry another.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-elton289_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton289-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Anne did not argue, and confirmed that the marriage had never been consummated.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick373_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick373-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Anne's previous betrothal to the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Lorraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Lorraine">Duke of Lorraine</a>'s son <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Duke_of_Lorraine" title="Francis I, Duke of Lorraine">Francis</a> provided further grounds for the annulment.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The marriage was subsequently dissolved, and Anne received the title of "The King's Sister", two houses and a generous allowance.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick373_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick373-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> It was soon clear that Henry had fallen for the 17-year-old <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Howard" title="Catherine Howard">Catherine Howard</a>, the Duke of Norfolk's niece, the politics of which worried Cromwell, for Norfolk was a political opponent.<sup id="cite_ref-elton289291_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton289291-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly after, the religious reformers (and protégés of Cromwell) <a href="/wiki/Robert_Barnes_(martyr)" title="Robert Barnes (martyr)">Robert Barnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Jerome_(martyr)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Jerome (martyr)">William Jerome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Garret" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Garret">Thomas Garret</a> were burned as heretics.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick373_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick373-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Cromwell, meanwhile, fell out of favour although it is unclear exactly why, for there is little evidence of differences of domestic or foreign policy. Despite his role, he was never formally accused of being responsible for Henry's failed marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick367377_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick367377-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Cromwell was now surrounded by enemies at court, with Norfolk also able to draw on his niece's position.<sup id="cite_ref-elton289291_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elton289291-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Cromwell was charged with treason, selling export licences, granting passports, and drawing up commissions without permission, and may also have been blamed for the failure of the foreign policy that accompanied the attempted marriage to Anne.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He was subsequently <a href="/wiki/Attainder" title="Attainder">attainted</a> and beheaded.<sup id="cite_ref-scarisbrick367377_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scarisbrick367377-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_to_Catherine_Howard">Marriage to Catherine Howard</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:366px;max-width:366px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Portrait_of_a_Lady,_perhaps_Katherine_Howard_(Royal_Collection).JPG" class="image"><img alt=""
